## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanics
**Analysis**: The task involves the relationship between stress (sigma) and strain (epsilon) at different temperatures (T), which is a fundamental problem in thermomechanics. In this domain, material properties such as elasticity, plasticity, and creep are typically described as functions of temperature.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear elastic behavior: sigma = c0 * epsilon (isotropic materials, low strains)
- Strain hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 (plastic materials, moderate strains)
- Arrhenius creep: epsilon = c0 * exp(-c1 / T) (temperature-dependent creep, low stresses)
- Thermal expansion: epsilon = c0 * (T - T_ref) (thermal expansion of materials)
- Viscoelastic relaxation: epsilon = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) + c2 * (1 - exp(-c3 * t)) (creep and relaxation in polymers)
- Zener relation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / (T - T_m)) (dynamic modulus and temperature)
- Schoeckly equation: epsilon = c0 * T + c1 * T**2 (anelastic behavior in materials)
- Boltzmann superposition principle: epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**2 (summation of elastic and plastic strains)
- Temperature-dependent Young's modulus: E = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (temperature-dependent stiffness of materials)
- Modified Arrhenius equation: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 / T) + c2 * epsilon (non-Arrhenius creep behavior in materials)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature sensitivity: as T approaches T_ref, c0 goes to zero, and c1 remains finite (in thermal expansion and anelastic behavior)
- Strain-rate sensitivity: c0 is large, c1 is small, and c2 is zero (in flow stress models and creep models)
- Power-law creep: c0 is finite, c1 is large, and c2 is zero (in high-temperature creep and viscoplasticity)
- Joule-Thomson expansion: as temperature approaches a critical value, material properties change drastically (in shockwave physics and supercritical fluid behavior)
- Viscoelastic memory: c0 and c1 are large, and c2 and c3 are small (in elastomers and high-temperature viscoelasticity)
